                            <div class="player-info-box-header "><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Carlos Beltran</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team">&nbsp;</div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 40</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: B/R</div>

        <div class="player-info-box-pos">OF</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>4/24/1977 (40 y, 10 m, 14 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=589&position=OF#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">1995 June Amateur Draft - Round: 2, Pick: 19, Overall: 49, Team: Kansas City Royals</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=589&position=OF#contract" >$16M / 1 Years (2017)</a>

            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>Despite hitting for limited power, Beltran was enjoying one of the finest seasons of his career last year before succumbing to injury.  He had a .952 OPS in late June, before finally landing on the disabled list for two and a half months with a bruised leg bone.  Beltran did return in September, but did not perform at his previous levels.  An excellent all-around player, Beltran is one of the top hitters in the game despite being a radically different player than he was a few years ago.  In 2006, Beltran had a .275/.388/.594 slash line.  Last year it was .325/.415/.500.  While Beltran’s walks fell off, so did his strikeouts.  His 1.09 BB/K last year ranked 12th amongst all players with at least 300 plate appearances.  Beltran still draws walks, but he is much more likely to swing early in the count.  In 2009 he saw an average of 3.65 pitches per plate appearance, down from 4.20 in 2006. <br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Coming into 2009, Beltran had been one of the most consistent fantasy performers over the previous three seasons.  But now there are a lot of question marks surrounding him.  Will the bone bruise linger?  And even if it doesn’t, what will Beltran give in average and homers?  Last year Beltran had a .353 BABIP, the highest mark of his career and 46 points above his lifetime mark.  The Dutton-Carty xBABIP estimator gave him a .309 mark, so we are likely to see a drop in average. Power-wise, Beltran declined in HR/FB ratio for the third straight season, down to 10.8%, the second lowest of his career since we have data in 2002.  His previous low came in 2005, when he had an 8.8% mark.  The following year he rebounded to post a 21.1% mark, the highest of his career.  Expect more home runs from Beltran as he adjusts to Citi Field, which ESPN gave a 1.057 park factor for homers. (Brian Joura)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Knee surgery struck down a once elite player, and now Beltran looks to try to salvage what’s left of his career while playing at less than full speed.  In his prime, Beltran nearly went 40-40, but he has been limited to just 14 stolen bases over the last two years as his knees have betrayed him.  He was able to retain more of his power, and could settle in as a still-productive 25 HR outfielder if he stays on the field with regularity, but his days as a duel threat are probably over.   Heading into the final year of his contract, the Mets have fewer incentives to play him every day, so if he struggles and the team falls out of the race, he could find himself on the bench in the second half.  There is some upside with Beltran, but he’s probably not a great source of steals anymore, and you could probably get a healthier outfielder with similar power and less name value for a lower price.   (Dave Cameron)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>A shell of what he once was, don't bid for Beltran on the assumption that he's going to reclaim past glory.  Knee surgery stole his speed and most of his fantasy value.  </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Beltran has the daunting task of helping replace Albert Pujols in St. Louis, but he won’t have to live up to those expectations to make him worthy of having on your fantasy team. He is still a dynamic offensive player when he’s healthy, and hopefully the Cardinals’ training staff will able to keep him on the field for at least 140 games in 2012. While the ballpark in St. Louis won’t help Beltran’s power numbers, hitters like Lance Berkman, Pujols, and Matt Holliday have shown it doesn’t have to completely put a damper on home runs. Look for Beltran to hit around .290 with 20 homers and at least 80 runs and RBI. While he’s no longer a top fantasy outfielder, his line should still be good enough to warrant a mid-round draft pick, especially in OBP leagues. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>"Blame" Beltran is still a dynamic offensive player when he’s healthy, and hopefully the Cardinals’ training staff will able to keep him on the field for at least 140 games in 2012. While he’s no longer a top fantasy outfielder, his line should still be good enough to warrant a mid-round draft pick, especially in OBP leagues.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>When Beltran remains healthy, he produces with the bat. His 32 home runs ranked in the Top 10 for outfielders, and his .225 ISO was his highest since 2007. He also benefits from a potent Cardinals lineup, which should allow him to drive in plenty of runs. Fantasy owners should perhaps be concerned about an uptick in his swinging-strike rate (6.6% to 9.3%) and decrease in his contact percentage (84.7% to 79.5%) -- both of which are career-worst marks for Beltran. Most of the damage came in July and August of last season, however, so it seems to be a mere blip on the radar, rather than a trend. If healthy, Beltran is a good bet to replicate his production from last year and should be one of the top 20 outfielders off the board in most drafts. (JP Breen)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Injury concerns will always linger -- especially as he moves into his age-36 season on wounded knees -- but Carlos Beltran should still be a solid second-tier outfielder who provides value in each of the five standard roto categories.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Beltran refuses to let the effects of aging cripple him, as he enjoyed another strong performance at the plate. And the Yankees took notice, signing the veteran and bringing him back to the Big Apple. But Beltran's speed is now gone and his walk rate has tumbled, proving that there are indeed some chinks in the armor. After some health issues in previous years, Beltran has remained on the field at a surprisingly high clip. Unfortunately, heading into his age-37 season, the risk of collapse increases greatly. He should remain fairly productive while on the field though, and the move to the significantly more hitter-friendly Yankee Stadium will help. Since he should hit in a good spot in his new lineup, his runs scored and runs batted in totals should remain at respectable levels. But age could take its toll at any time, which could cut into both his performance and his playing time. (<a href="https://twitter.com/MikePodhorzer" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Beltran continues to remain productive at the plate despite his advanced age. A move to the second-best home run park for left-handers will curb the downside, but with his speed disappearing, he's a serious risk for fantasy owners to take on.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>It's never easy to watch formerly great players decline, but that's exactly what 2014 looked like for Carlos Beltran. After signing a three-year deal with the Yankees, Beltran limped around the outfield and posting some of the worst numbers of his career. His .233/.301/.402 line in just 449 plate appearances features similar walk and strikeout rates to his 2013, only without all the power. Pitchers worked him more and more with hard stuff, suggesting he owned a slower bat. As always with an older player, there is injury information to weigh. Beltran had surgery to remove bone spurs and loose bodies from this right elbow, a painful injury that surely inhibited his ability to drive the ball. When he was mostly healthy in 2013, he was a different player than Beltran at his peak. He walked less, struck out more, and didn't glide around the field as a bulkier corner outfielder. The what ifs are considerable with a player with this track record and mileage. Beltran can produce well above average, hitting for power from both sides of the plate. Or he could miss chunks of time and look every day of his 38 years as he struggles to hit premium velocity. This is the tantalizing nature of veteran players -- you aren't alone if you fall under their spell. (Drew Fairservice)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Slowed by injuries and age, is there anything left in Carlos Beltran's bat?</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The skills have eroded for the once great Beltran, but like a few of his elderly Yankee teammates, he had a resurgent 2015. After cratering to a 96 weighted runs created plus in 2014, Beltran improved to a 119 wRC+ last season. The projections suggest Beltran will be above average in 2016, while still taking a dip from last year's numbers. Although Beltran made his bones as a two-way player, he can't really play the field anymore. Normally, a player in Beltran's situation would move to first base or designated hitter, but with Alex Rodriguez and Mark Teixeira in the fold, Beltran will likely stay in right field. However, Aaron Judge, one of the top Yankees prospects, plays that position and finished last season in Triple-A. Additionally, the Yankees acquired outfielder Aaron Hicks. In the last season of his contract with the Yankees, Beltran can't afford to struggle too much as they have plenty of directions to turn to. Beltran can still hit right handed pitchers as he's had a wRC+ of 127, 119 and 143 the last three years against them. It's been the opposite against lefties though, as he's put up a disappointing wRC+ of 99, 51 and 100 versus south paws over the same time frame. (Ben Pasinkoff)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Considering his glove, the Yankees have better options to play against lefties and even if he's healthy all year. Beltran will likely find himself with fewer at bats this season. Beltran can likely provide some value as a bench outfielder. but I wouldn't expect a full season from him.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>If Beltran keeps hitting the way he hit in 2016, the discussion regarding his Hall of Fame chances will shift from "if" to "when." After three years of faring relatively poorly against southpaws, he punished them last year, fully reviving the idea that he's still a plenty-effective full-time hitter. A jam-packed outfield situation in Houston will allow him to enjoy the perks of being a designated hitter; the extra rest, one might think, could help stave off injury and keep the dreaded aging curve at bay a bit longer. In light of the league-wide power surge, it's difficult to determine the legitimacy of many home run outputs, including Beltran's. Given his age and history, a return to a more modest home run rate seems predestined, although I doubt anyone feels entitled to a repeat. His type comes a dime a dozen nowadays, but 20 home runs and a .270 batting average gets the job done, even in standard formats. There may be safer options, but the Astros' potent lineup should bolster his stock. He's a fringe top-50 outfielder. (Alex Chamberlain)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Beltran, 39, just posted his fifth OPS above .800 in the last six years. The power should slip back to its more recent levels, but his anticipated role as Houston's designated hitter should help keep him fresh. He's a fringe starting outfielder in standard formats, and Houston's potent lineup should prop him up.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>

However, Aaron Judge, one of the top Yankees prospects, plays that position and finished last season in Triple-A. Additionally, the Yankees acquired outfielder Aaron Hicks. In the last season of his contract with the Yankees, Beltran can't afford to struggle too much as they have plenty of directions to turn to. Beltran can still hit right handed pitchers as he's had a wRC+ of 127, 119 and 143 the last three years against them. It's been the opposite against lefties though, as he's put up a disappointing wRC+ of 99, 51 and 100 versus south paws over the same time frame. (Ben Pasinkoff)",

A jam-packed outfield situation in Houston will allow him to enjoy the perks of being a designated hitter; the extra rest, one might think, could help stave off injury and keep the dreaded aging curve at bay a bit longer. In light of the league-wide power surge, it's difficult to determine the legitimacy of many home run outputs, including Beltran's. Given his age and history, a return to a more modest home run rate seems predestined, although I doubt anyone feels entitled to a repeat. His type comes a dime a dozen nowadays, but 20 home runs and a .270 batting average gets the job done, even in standard formats.
